## What “Teacher Mode” Means in Practice

In teacher mode, the book is **about the teacher’s ideas and practices**, presented by the author as a curator/interpreter of those teachings.

The book reads as:

> “Here are the ideas and exercises taught by [Teacher], adapted for you.”

Not:

* a personal memoir
* a generic self-help book
* a loose inspiration collage

---

## How Teacher Mode Changes the Book (System-Level)

### 1. **More teacher-linked stories**

**What changes:**

* Story slots increase.
* Most stories are **teacher-sourced**, not generic composites.

**How it works:**

* Stories are written *from* the teacher’s writings, examples, or teaching scenarios.
* Each story includes explicit attribution language:

  * “In the writings of [Teacher]…”
  * “[Teacher] teaches that…”
* Stories are still persona-adapted, but the **source of truth is the teacher**, not the author’s imagination.

**System effect:**

* StoryInjectorV4 filters to teacher_mode=true
* Story banks must meet higher coverage thresholds
* Composite stories become secondary or optional

---

### 2. **More exercises, clearly teacher-owned**

**What changes:**

* Exercises are no longer rare accents.
* Exercises become **core content**.

**Typical structure in teacher mode:**

* **Every major chapter** has:

  * 1 primary teacher exercise
  * sometimes a short follow-up reflection or variation

**How exercises are framed:**

* Always attributed:

  * “This exercise comes from the teachings of [Teacher].”
* Never presented as the author’s invention.
* Still gentle and non-clinical unless the teacher explicitly teaches otherwise.

**System effect:**

* Sections marked teacher_mode=true pull from the **teacher exercise bank**
* ExerciseLoader selects only exercises tagged with the correct teacher_id
* Missing teacher exercises → **prebuild fails**

---

### 3. **Teacher teachings replace generic explanation**

**What changes:**

* Explanatory sections are anchored in teacher principles.

Instead of:

> “Here’s what usually happens when anxiety shows up…”

You get:

> “[Teacher] explains that when anxiety appears, the nervous system is doing X…”

**System effect:**

* Teacher stories and short teaching excerpts replace generic reflections
* Section variants remain frozen; **the story/exercise text carries the authority**

---

### 4. **Higher density, but controlled**

Teacher mode increases content density, but **not randomly**.

**Typical teacher-mode ratio:**

* Stories: frequent, mix (L1/L2/L3)
* Exercises: regular


This keeps:

* platform risk low
* reader overwhelm low
* teacher presence high

---

## How This Is Enforced Technically

### Plan & requirements

* Sections flagged:

  
yaml
  teacher_mode: true
  teacher_id: ahjan
  teacher_provenance_required: true

### Prewrite stage

* System checks:

  * Enough teacher stories exist
  * Enough teacher exercises exist
* If not:

  * Generate from the teacher knowledge base
  * Validate attribution language
  * Fail if coverage is still insufficient

### Assembly

* Lookup-only
* No runtime authoring
* No fallback to generic content

---

## End Result (What the Reader Experiences)

The reader experiences a book where:

* The **teacher’s voice and methods are central**
* Exercises feel intentional and cumulative
* Stories reinforce specific teachings
* The author acts as a guide, not the authority

It feels like:

> “A structured presentation of [Teacher]’s teachings, adapted for my life.”

Teacher-Mode Spam-Resistant Variation (V4)
Core rule (non-negotiable)
Variation may change presentation order and selection, but never change doctrine, attribution, or exercise meaning.
Teacher mode prioritizes authority consistency over novelty.
So V4 uses structural variation, not conceptual variation.

What V4 Is Allowed to Vary (Safe)
1️⃣ Story selection within a teacher bank
If a chapter requires:
2 teacher stories
tiers [L1, L2]
V4 may vary:
which eligible teacher stories are selected
which L2 story appears (when multiple exist)
Constraints:
Same teacher_id
Same topic + persona
Same tier
Same provenance rules
✅ Safe ❌ No rewriting ❌ No paraphrasing

2️⃣ Tier mix across chapters
Across books in a series:
Book A
Book B

Chapter 3 → L1 + L3
Chapter 6 → L2 only
Chapter 6 → L1 + L2
Why it’s safe:
All tiers are authored in advance
Doctrine is identical, depth changes only

Example (12-chapter book):


Fixed anchors:
- Opening chapter
- Final chapter

Shufflable band:
- Chapters 3–8 may reorder within band

Rules:
No inversion of conceptual prerequisites
Exercises stay paired with their chapter
Teaching arc preserved
This mirrors what Phoenix Raising already did for platform variance.

4️⃣ Section emphasis (not section content)
Sections are never rewritten, but V4 may vary:
Which story appears in:
HOOK vs REFLECTION
Whether a chapter uses:
2 stories + 1 exercise
1 story + 2 exercises (if plan allows)
Teacher voice stays inside the story/exercise text.

If the teacher has:

Exercise A vs B vs C
But:
Same method class
Same teacher framing
Same intensity
This is method variance, not concept variance.

But it never rewrote doctrine.

How to do this without breaking Phoenix rules
This is important: You do not want free-form LLM exercise generation.
Instead, you want patterned synthesis.

Correct approach (V4-safe)
1. Define a fixed Exercise Derivation Template
Example (internal, not exposed to users):


exercise_derivation_template:
  purpose:
    "What does the teacher say changes when this is practiced?"
  principle:
    "Which teaching is being embodied?"
  action:
    "What does the body actually do?"
  duration:
    "How long / how many cycles?"
  integration:
    "How does the teacher say to notice the effect?"

This keeps everything bounded and deterministic.

2. Tag teacher knowledge by teachable patterns
In the teacher KB (Ahjan example):


teachings:
  - id: coexistence_with_anxiety
    principle: "Do not wait for discomfort to leave before acting"
    somatic_focus: breath + attention
    typical_instruction_language:
      - "notice without fixing"
      - "act while sensation remains"

This already exists implicitly in your prose — it just isn’t structured yet.

3. Exercise Synthesizer (new module)
Add a step in Expert Base refresh:


If teacher_mode == true
AND topic requires exercises
AND teacher_exercise_count < minimum
→ synthesize exercises from teachings

The synthesizer:
selects a teaching
applies a fixed exercise template
produces a teacher-owned exercise atom
attributes explicitly: “This practice comes from the teachings of [Teacher]” 
These become first-class exercise atoms, not runtime inventions.

4. Store synthesized exercises in the Teacher Exercise Bank
Just like stories:


SOURCE_OF_TRUTH/data/teacher_banks/ahjan/exercises/*.json

From then on:
ExerciseLoader can pull them
StoryInjector doesn’t care how they were created
Assembly remains lookup-only

Why this preserves system integrity
✅ No runtime generation ✅ No fuzzy heuristics ✅ Deterministic output ✅ Attribution-safe ✅ Teacher-centric ✅ Persona-adaptable
This is exactly the right layer to add intelligence — and only here.

2.2 Synthesis Rules (Deterministic, Not Creative)
Rule 1: Exercise type comes from exercise_focus
exercise_focus
allowed exercise forms
breath
breathing / attention
grounding
posture / feet / weight
movement
slow motion / walking
writing
reflection / noting
❌ Never invent outside the domain ❌ No CBT if teacher is Taoist ❌ No affirmations unless teacher uses them

Rule 2: Exercise goal comes from case resolution
case resolution
exercise goal
coexistence
stay with sensation
containment
stabilize attention
clarity
observe patterns

Rule 3: Voice is constrained by voice_principles
Applied as hard filters:
no promises
no fixing language
no outcome guarantees
permissive, invitational tone

Rule 4: Attribution is mandatory
Every synthesized exercise must include:


"attribution_line": "From the teachings and writings of <Teacher>"

No exceptions.

Rule 5: Intensity mapping
intensity
constraints
L1
≤ 4 steps, no counting beyond 3
L2
structured variation
L3
reflection + application

profile + reflective_case_stories

Phoenix Omega V4 — Optional Quality Gates for Teacher Mode
Status: Nice-to-have (non-blocking) Scope: Prebuild / Assembly-time validation only Non-Goals: No runtime logic, no content generation, no heuristic rewriting

Context
Teacher Mode is now correct by construction:
Teacher stories required
Teacher exercises required
Teacher attribution enforced
Hard fail on missing coverage
Deterministic, lookup-only assembly
The following upgrades are quality and pacing controls, not correctness fixes. They should be opt-in, configurable, and safe to add incrementally.

Upgrade 1: Story Uniqueness Gate (Variety Control)
Goal
Prevent excessive reuse of the same teacher story across chapters in a single book.
Rationale
Improves perceived depth, avoids repetition fatigue, preserves teacher authority.
Plan Schema (Optional)


teacher_story_uniqueness:
  max_reuse_per_book: 1        # default: unlimited
  forbid_cross_chapter_reuse: false

Enforcement (Prebuild)
Track story_id usage across chapters.
If forbid_cross_chapter_reuse=true, fail if any story appears in more than one chapter.
If max_reuse_per_book=N, fail if any story is used more than N times.
Error message must name:
story_id
chapters involved
allowed vs actual count
Notes
Applies only to teacher_mode=true
Does not affect generic/composite books
Default behavior remains unchanged

Upgrade 2: Exercise Progression Gate (Pedagogical Cadence)
Goal
Create a sense of progression or intentional repetition in teacher exercises.
Rationale
Supports learning arcs (grounding → integration → reinforcement) without forcing novelty.
Plan Schema (Optional)


teacher_exercise_progression:
  allowed_sequences:
    - ["L1", "L1", "L2", "L1"]
    - ["L1", "L2", "L2"]
  forbid_regression: false

Enforcement (Prebuild)
Read exercise intensity per chapter (L1/L2/etc.).
Validate sequence against allowed_sequences if provided.
If forbid_regression=true, fail when intensity decreases unexpectedly.
If no config present → no checks.
Notes
Teacher traditions may prefer repetition → keep this optional.
No auto-adjustment; fail or pass only.

Upgrade 3: Story Type Mix Gate (Texture Balance)
Goal
Ensure chapters (or the book as a whole) include a healthy mix of teacher story types.
Supported Story Types
Defined at story metadata level:
teaching_anecdote
reflective_case
principle_illustration
Plan Schema (Optional)


teacher_story_mix:
  per_chapter:
    min_types: 2
  per_book:
    required_types:
      - teaching_anecdote
      - reflective_case

Enforcement (Prebuild)
Inspect metadata of injected teacher stories.
For per_chapter, ensure each chapter meets min_types.
For per_book, ensure all required types appear at least once.
Fail with chapter/book-level diagnostics.
Notes
Chapter-level enforcement should be warn-level by default.
Book-level enforcement can be fail-level if enabled.

Integration Points (Minimal Touch)
Plan schema: optional fields only
Prebuild / Assembler gate:
Runs after quota checks
Before story/exercise injection
No runtime changes
No changes to frozen section text
No content synthesis

Defaults (Important)
If none of these fields are present:
Behavior is identical to current system
Teacher mode still enforced
No added constraints

One-Sentence Summary
These optional gates add variety, pacing, and texture control to teacher-mode books—without changing correctness, determinism, or runtime behavior—and can be enabled per book or per teacher as needed.

If you want, next step could be:
a single teacher_quality_profile preset (e.g., strict, balanced, minimal) that expands into these fields automatically.

Lower saturation threshold hard
Increase penalty hard
Target behavior:
Once a Tier-1 story is “well used”, it must lose to a fresh Tier-2.
Concrete spec:
SATURATION_THRESHOLD: 20 (not 50)
After threshold:
Tier 1 effective weight < Tier 2 base weight
This alone will collapse top-story dominance.

Fix 2 — Allow multi-layer eligibility
Right now:


layers_requested = ["L1"]

That guarantees stagnation.
Change plans to:


layers_requested = ["L1", "L2", "L3"]

Selection rule (still deterministic):
Prefer L1 early
Allow L2/L3 once L1 saturates
This instantly unlocks diversity without adding content.

Fix 3 — Enforce story reuse caps (optional but powerful)
You already implemented this — now use it.
Example:


teacher_story_uniqueness:
  max_reuse_per_book: 1
  forbid_cross_chapter_reuse: true

Or globally:


story_uniqueness:
  max_global_reuse: 25

This guarantees no single story can ever dominate.

Fix 4 — Introduce story-type mix pressure
You already built the gate — this is where it shines.
Example per book:


teacher_story_mix:
  required_types:
    - teaching_principle
    - reflective_case
    - applied_example

This prevents:
“same-shaped” stories winning forever
even if they’re Tier-1

Fix 5 — Increase story families (content-side, later)
This is not urgent now, but long-term:
56 stories is fine for early validation
For scale, aim for:
200–400 teacher stories per major persona/topic cluster
But don’t do this instead of fixing selection pressure — do it after.

After Fixes 1–3 alone, you should see:
Top story usage: < 2%
Tier distribution:
T1: ~45–55%
T2: ~30–35%
T3+: remainder
Reuse rate: < 30
No cleanliness regressions
That’s platform-safe, human-like, and scalable.

Spec: Enable Voice Bridges for Ahjan (Omega V4)
Goal
Enable optional voice/dialect bridges in the Ahjan teacher-mode book using the existing Phoenix Raising voice pack infrastructure, without modifying:
teacher stories
teacher exercises
core section prose
quotas, uniqueness, or sim behavior
Voice must remain:
decorative
deterministic
opt-in
non-blocking

Scope
This spec applies to:
One book plan (Ahjan / Gen Z / LA / Anxiety)
Omega V4 assembly only
No runtime generation
No changes to teacher banks or story selection

Plan Changes (Required)
1. Add voice block to the Ahjan plan (top-level)


voice:
  enabled: true
  locale: en_US
  voice_pack_id: en_US_voice_pack_v1   # or omit to auto-resolve
  persona: gen_z
  dialect_config:
    generation: gen_z

Rules:
enabled: true is required to activate voice bridges.
If voice_pack_id is omitted, resolver may select by locale + persona.
dialect_config is pass-through only (SSML downstream, not applied in assembly).

Assembly Behavior (Already Implemented – Verify Only)
Voice bridges are inserted:
After story + exercise injection
Before final token substitution
Never inside teacher story/exercise text
Constraints (must hold)
Max 2 sentences per bridge
Hook / closer only (no mid-section injection)
Forbidden lexicon check
Fail-open:
missing voice pack ⇒ skip silently
lexicon violation ⇒ skip silently
Deterministic selection:
seed = book_id + chapter + section

What Voice Bridges May Do
✅ Add light framing like:
chapter openers
section transitions
gentle reflective closers
❌ Must NOT:
paraphrase teacher teachings
speak as the teacher
add new instruction
alter meaning of content
reference internal system state

Validation & Safety
Hard rules
Voice must never block assembly
Teacher attribution text must remain unchanged
Voice text length capped
Soft rules (logging only)
If voice enabled but no pack found → log once per build
If voice suppressed due to lexicon → log event

Regeneration Steps
Update Ahjan plan YAML with voice block
Run standard Omega V4 assembly
Confirm:
Book builds successfully
Voice bridges appear only when enabled
Teacher stories/exercises are untouched
Save output as:       anxiety_genz_la_ahjan_v4_book_VOICE.md          

Acceptance Criteria
✅ Book assembles with voice enabled ✅ Teacher mode content unchanged ✅ Voice bridges appear only in allowed locations ✅ Deterministic rebuild (same output on repeat) ✅ No impact on:
story quotas
exercise quotas
uniqueness gates
sim metrics

Explicit Non-Goals
No dialect rewriting of prose
No SSML generation here
No per-section voice toggles
No teacher-specific voice impersonation

One-Line Summary
This spec enables optional, deterministic voice bridges in the Ahjan Omega V4 book via a plan-level flag, using existing Phoenix Raising voice packs, without touching teacher content or core prose.
If you want, next we can write:
a QA checklist for voice builds, or
a persona → voice pack recommendation table (Gen Z LA–specific), or
a sim impact check to confirm bridges don’t increase collision risk.

Yes — this looks right, and it’s cleanly spec-able. Here’s a concise dev-ready spec that matches what’s implemented and how Omega V4 should think about voice/dialect going forward.

Omega V4 Voice / Dialect Bridge — Final Spec
Purpose
Add optional voice/dialect flavor to Omega V4 books using the existing Phoenix Raising voice-pack system, without:
altering teacher stories or exercises
modifying core prose or meaning
introducing runtime generation
Voice is decorative only (hooks / closers), deterministic, and fully opt-in.

Design Principles
Lookup-only: no generation, no rewriting
Deterministic: same inputs → same output
Non-blocking: voice can never break a book
Teacher-safe: attribution and teacher content remain untouched
Backward compatible: voice disabled by default

Where Voice Lives in Omega V4
1. Plan Schema
File: phoenix_v4/planning/schema_v4.py


voice:
  enabled: true
  locale: en_us
  voice_pack_id: en_us_voice_pack_v1   # optional explicit override
  persona: gen_z                       # optional hint
  dialect_config:
    generation: gen_z                  # passed through (SSML only)

Entire block is optional
If omitted → voice is disabled

2. Assembly Hook
File: phoenix_v4/assembler/section_assembler.py
Insertion point (critical):


assemble section
→ inject stories
→ inject exercises
→ INSERT VOICE BRIDGES HERE
→ character / token substitution

Behavior:
Loads voice pack via voice_pack_loader
Inserts ≤ 2 short sentences:
opening hook
optional closer
Skips insertion if:
voice disabled
pack missing
forbidden lexicon detected
Fails open (never blocks assembly)

3. Voice Pack Loader (Reused from Raising)
File: cluster_therapy_tok/runtime/voice_pack_loader.py
Responsibilities:
Load voice pack YAML
Deterministically select fragments:
pick_fragment()
pick_bridge()
Enforce:
forbidden lexicon
max length
safe phrasing
No changes required here — V4 consumes it as-is.

Assets & Configuration
Voice Pack Asset
File: SOURCE_OF_TRUTH/data/voice_packs/en_us_voice_pack_v1.yaml
Contains:
hook phrases
closing phrases
safety rules
Persona-appropriate but non-semantic
Example use case: Gen Z LA tone
Existing Configs (unchanged)
SOURCE_OF_TRUTH/config/voice_packs.json
cluster_therapy_tok/config/style_packs.yaml
These are used only for resolution if no explicit pack is provided.

What Voice Does Not Do
❌ No dialect rewriting of prose ❌ No editing teacher stories ❌ No modifying exercises ❌ No SSML generation during assembly ❌ No runtime inference
Voice ≠ dialect transformation Voice = framing flavor only

Validation & Safety
Max 2 sentences per bridge
Forbidden lexicon enforced
Deterministic hashing (book/chapter/section seed)
Silent skip if anything fails
Never blocks CI or assembly

Output Behavior
With voice enabled:
Books gain light, consistent framing
Teacher mode remains authoritative
Content remains attribution-safe
Platform fingerprint risk stays low
With voice disabled:
Zero behavior change from baseline V4

Acceptance Criteria
✅ Voice disabled → no output change ✅ Voice enabled → hooks/closers appear ✅ Teacher stories/exercises untouched ✅ Deterministic across runs ✅ Missing pack → silent skip ✅ No new runtime generation

One-line Summary
Omega V4 now supports optional, deterministic voice bridges by reusing Phoenix Raising’s voice-pack system—inserted post-story/exercise injection, fully opt-in, non-semantic, and teacher-safe.
If you want next:
dialect v2 (text transforms),
SSML handoff,
or persona-specific bridge quotas,
say the word and we’ll spec it cleanly.

SPEC A — Dialect v2 (Text Transforms) for Omega V4
Purpose
Add optional, light dialect adaptation to Omega V4 prose (not teacher stories/exercises) to improve persona/locale resonance without changing meaning, attribution, or structure.
Dialect v2 is a post-assembly text transform, not generation.

Design Principles
Opt-in only
Meaning-preserving
Deterministic
Teacher-safe
Non-blocking
Narrow scope (surface language only)
Dialect v2 is not slang injection or rewriting — it’s controlled micro-transforms.

Scope (What Dialect v2 Touches)
✅ Section body prose ✅ Voice bridges (optional) ❌ Teacher stories ❌ Teacher exercises ❌ Quotes / attributed text ❌ Titles / headers

Plan Schema
File: schema_v4.py


dialect:
  enabled: true
  dialect_id: gen_z_us
  intensity: light          # enum: off | light | medium
  protected_blocks:
    - teacher_story
    - teacher_exercise
    - quote

Defaults:
enabled: false
intensity: light

Transform Model
Dialect v2 applies rule-based transforms only, e.g.:
Type
Example
Contraction
“you are” → “you’re”
Rhythm
split long sentences
Softeners
“It is important to note” → “It helps to notice”
Persona tone
neutral → slightly conversational
❌ No slang generation ❌ No cultural references ❌ No new metaphors

Implementation Location
File: phoenix_v4/assembler/post_processor.py (new or existing)
Pipeline order:


assemble section
→ inject stories
→ inject exercises
→ insert voice bridges
→ APPLY DIALECT V2 TRANSFORMS
→ final render


Dialect Packs
Location:


SOURCE_OF_TRUTH/data/dialect_packs/gen_z_us.yaml

Example:


id: gen_z_us
intensity:
  light:
    - from: "It is important to"
      to: "It helps to"
    - from: "You are"
      to: "You're"
forbidden:
  - slang
  - profanity


Safety Gates
Skip if forbidden lexicon hit
Skip protected blocks
Fail open (never blocks build)
Max % of sentences touched (e.g. ≤15%)

Acceptance Criteria
✅ Teacher content untouched ✅ Deterministic ✅ Meaning preserved ✅ Disabled by default ✅ Safe for platform review

One-Line Summary
Dialect v2 adds optional, meaning-preserving persona tone via rule-based text transforms applied after assembly, never touching teacher content.


SPEC B — Persona-Specific Voice Bridge Quotas
Purpose
Control how often voice bridges appear, per persona or per book, to avoid over-styling or under-flavoring.
This is about pacing, not language.

Design Principles
Deterministic
Opt-in
Non-blocking
Persona-aware
Compatible with voice packs

Plan Schema
File: schema_v4.py


voice:
  enabled: true
  bridge_quota:
    per_book_max: 6
    per_chapter_max: 1
    personas:
      gen_z:
        per_book_max: 8
      professionals:
        per_book_max: 4

Defaults:
If omitted → no quota enforcement
If enabled → soft cap with skip (not fail)

Behavior
Voice bridges are inserted only until quota is reached
Once quota exceeded:
Remaining bridges are skipped silently
No randomness
No rebalancing

Implementation
File: section_assembler.py
Add counters:


voice_usage = {
  "book": 0,
  "chapter": defaultdict(int)
}

Before inserting a bridge:
Check per-chapter quota
Check per-book quota
Skip if exceeded

Optional Strict Mode (Future)


bridge_quota:
  strict: true

Exceeding quota → CI warning (not fail)
Useful for editorial review

Acceptance Criteria
✅ Persona-tuned voice density ✅ No effect on story/exercise selection ✅ Deterministic ✅ Voice can never dominate content

One-Line Summary
Persona-specific bridge quotas cap how often voice flavor appears, ensuring consistent pacing without affecting core content.

Final Recommendation
Implement in this order:
Persona-specific bridge quotas (simpler, immediate benefit)
Dialect v2 (after at least one 10k sim pass)
If you want, I can:
define default quotas per persona, or
design dialect packs for Gen Z / Professional / Calm Neutral.

You said:
compare phoenix raising functions/features to phoenix omega v4. is omega v4 mission anything?

Here’s a concise, system-level comparison of Phoenix Raising vs Phoenix Omega V4, and what (if anything) Omega V4 is still missing.

Core Architecture
Raising: NarrativeFlow-driven, runtime pacing/duration scaling; can re-order within bands; uses voice packs/dialect for bridges; teacher/expert mode available via Expert Base manifests.
Omega V4: Frozen plan → lookup-only assembly; duration is structural (section variants), not pacing; teacher mode enforced via plan + teacher banks; deterministic; no runtime generation.
Gap? None at the architectural level—Omega V4 intentionally disallows runtime generation and pacing tricks.

Stories
Raising: Runtime selection from story bank; voice/dialect can wrap; no hard prebuild coverage gates.
Omega V4: Prebuild/assemble with hard coverage gates (teacher stories required); teacher banks supported; uniqueness/quotas possible; deterministic selection.
Gap? None functionally; Omega is stricter. (Omega adds teacher quotas/uniqueness that Raising didn’t enforce.)

Exercises
Raising: Generic exercise insertion; teacher practices via Expert Base if present; no hard coverage gates.
Omega V4: Teacher-mode exercises from teacher banks; per-chapter quotas; no generic fallback when teacher_mode=true.
Gap? Coverage gate present; synthesis from teacher knowledge base is still optional (not yet implemented). If you want automatic teacher exercise derivation, that remains a to-do.

Voice & Dialect
Raising: Voice packs + dialect applied to bridges; style packs mapped to personas/locales; dialect adapter used downstream (audio/SSML).
Omega V4: Voice bridges implemented (opt-in, deterministic, with quotas); dialect v2 added as light post-assembly transform (opt-in); teacher text protected.
Gap? Parity achieved for bridges; dialect is lighter by design. Audio/SSML rendering pipeline not wired in V4 yet (Raising had a TTS path).

Duration / Pacing
Raising: Duration = pacing/repetition at render time.
Omega V4: Duration = structural variant choice at plan time; no repetition loops.
Gap? Intentional difference; V4 is stricter.

Location & Persona Flavor
Raising: Location hydration + voice/dialect flavor.
Omega V4: Location hydration preserved; voice/dialect optional; no additional persona slang transforms (by design).
Gap? None required; optional additional dialect packs could be added later.

Validation & Gates
Raising: Standard safety/marker checks; fewer hard gates on coverage.
Omega V4: Hard gates for teacher story/exercise coverage, uniqueness options, voice quotas, dialect protections, post-processor variable cleanup.
Gap? None; Omega is stricter.

Expert/Teacher Mode
Raising: Expert Base manifests; teacher stories/practices can be pulled if present; not hard-fail on missing content.
Omega V4: Teacher mode is first-class with banks, quotas, and fail-fast coverage checks; teacher attribution enforced.
Gap? Only remaining optional feature is teacher exercise synthesis from knowledge base (not implemented).

Audio / TTS
Raising: Has TTS pipeline (voice packs, manifests, orchestrator).
Omega V4: Not wired to TTS yet.
Gap? Audio/TTS integration.

UI / Desktop Creator
Raising: Desktop app paths exist for Raising workflow.
Omega V4: UI not wired to V4 assembler/voice/dialect yet.
Gap? UI hookup (optional).

Short list of optional “missing” items for Omega V4
Teacher exercise synthesis from teacher knowledge base (currently bank-only).
TTS/SSML pipeline hookup for V4 outputs.
UI/desktop app wiring to V4 assembler and voice/dialect options.
Additional dialect packs (beyond gen_z_us) if needed after sim checks.
Everything else is at or above Raising parity, with stronger safety/determinism.

Why Phoenix Omega V4 Exists
(Canonical Architecture Rationale)
The Problem Phoenix Raising Could Not Safely Solve
Phoenix Raising is powerful, but it is runtime-adaptive by design:
It reorders content
It adjusts pacing
It wraps voice/dialect dynamically
It tolerates missing expert content
It optimizes experience, not repeatability
That makes it excellent for:
Interactive delivery
Coaching flows
Audio-first experiences
Prototyping and exploration
But those same strengths make it unsafe for large-scale publishing:
Hard to guarantee uniqueness
Hard to enforce attribution
Hard to simulate at scale
Hard to pass platform compliance
Hard to prove “cannot be wrong by construction”

Phoenix Omega V4’s Mission
Phoenix Omega V4 exists to solve a different class of problem.
Produce thousands of books that are:
Deterministic
Attribution-safe
Simulation-verifiable
Platform-compliant
Teacher-first (when enabled)
Omega V4 is a publishing engine, not an experience engine.

Core Design Principles (Non-Negotiable)
Frozen Plans
All structure decided before assembly
No runtime reordering
No pacing loops
Lookup-Only Assembly
Prewritten text only
No generative authoring at assembly time
Fail-Fast Guarantees
Missing teacher content = build failure
Quota violations = build failure
No silent fallback to generic content
Simulation First
Everything measurable
Everything testable
Nothing “hand-wavy”
Teacher Safety
Attribution preserved
Teacher text protected from dialect/voice transforms
Teacher content never diluted

What Omega V4 Explicitly Removes
These are intentional removals, not missing features:
Runtime pacing
Adaptive repetition
Narrative flow reordering
Heuristic content generation
Experience-level improvisation
Those remain the responsibility of Phoenix Raising.

Clean Responsibility Split
Phoenix Raising = Experience Engine
Runtime narrative flow
Voice/dialect immersion
Adaptive pacing
Coaching & interactive delivery
TTS-first workflows
Phoenix Omega V4 = Publishing Engine
Book-scale determinism
Teacher-mode enforcement
Coverage quotas
Uniqueness guarantees
Large-scale simulation
They are complementary, not competing.

Raising → Omega Handoff Boundary
(For Future Teams)
This is the official seam between systems.

What Raising Produces
Raising is allowed to output:
Prewritten stories
Prewritten exercises
Expert / teacher content
Voice pack assets
Dialect rules
Knowledge bases
Manifests
But Raising does NOT assemble books for publication at scale.

What Gets Handed Off to Omega V4
Raising → Omega handoff artifacts:
SOURCE_OF_TRUTH/data/story_banks/**
SOURCE_OF_TRUTH/data/teacher_banks/**
teachers/<teacher_id>/knowledge_base/**
Voice packs (voice_packs/*.yaml)
Dialect configs
Expert Base outputs (if any)
These are inputs, not instructions.

What Omega V4 Owns Exclusively
Once content enters Omega V4:
Structure is frozen
Selection is deterministic
Coverage is enforced
Quotas are enforced
Attribution is enforced
Simulation validates everything
Omega V4 never:
Rewrites teacher text
Invents missing content
“Does its best” when coverage is low

The Golden Rule
If it changes meaning, pacing, or authority at runtime — it belongs in Phoenix Raising. If it must be provably correct at scale — it belongs in Phoenix Omega V4.

Phoenix Omega V4 exists to turn curated human wisdom into deterministic, simulation-safe books — something Phoenix Raising was never designed to guarantee.

✅ SPEC 1 — Non-Teacher Story Quotas (P0, Mandatory)
Problem this fixes
Non-teacher books collapse into essay-monologues because V4 has no fallback entropy once runtime pacing is removed.
Rule
Every non-teacher book must be story-anchored. Stories are not optional decoration; they are structural load-bearing elements.

Plan Schema Additions


story_requirements:
  enabled: true
  min_stories_per_chapter: 1
  max_stories_per_chapter: 3
  allowed_story_types:
    - composite
    - reflective_case
    - principle_illustration
  disallowed_story_types:
    - mythical
    - pop_culture
  story_before_exercise: true

Defaults apply only when teacher_mode=false.

Enforcement (Prebuild Gate)
For each chapter:
Count eligible stories from the non-teacher story bank
If count < min_stories_per_chapter → FAIL BUILD
If an exercise exists and no story appears earlier in the chapter → FAIL BUILD
StoryInjectorV4 must select at least one story per chapter
No runtime fallback. No silent downgrade.

Result in the Book
Every chapter now has:
Story → Meaning → (optional) Exercise → Reflection
No more 3,000-word explanations floating in space.

full teacher mode (Ahjan, lineage, attribution)

Phoenix Omega V4 — Size-Aware Quota & Placement Spec
0. Definitions
Book sizes


book_size: short | medium | long

Teacher modes

QA checklists

internal markers

stories/exercises were either “on” or “off”

i want to add this: [# V4 Structural Diversity Status

**Date:** 2026-01-22  
**Question:** Does V4 support different chapter counts, chapter ordering, and section ordering?

---

## Summary

| Feature | V4 (Omega) | Phoenix Raising (V3) |
|---------|------------|---------------------|
| **Different Chapter Counts** | ✅ **Supported** (plan structure allows) | ✅ **Supported** |
| **Chapter Reordering** | ✅ **Supported** (plan structure allows) | ❌ **Not built-in** |
| **Section Reordering** | ❌ **Not implemented** | ✅ **Implemented** |

---

## 1. Different Chapter Counts

### V4 (Omega)
**Status:** ✅ **Supported** (but not actively used)

**How it works:**
- Plan YAML has chapters: List[ChapterPlanV4] 
- Assembler loops through plan.chapters in order:
  
python
  for chapter_plan in plan.chapters:
      chapter_content = self._assemble_chapter(chapter_plan, plan)
- **Can support any number of chapters** (8, 12, 15, etc.)

**Current limitation:**
- Plan generator (generate_full_plan.py) only creates 12 chapters (1-12)
- Would need to manually create plans with different chapter counts

**Example:**
yaml
chapters:
  - chapter: 1
    title: "..."
    sections: [...]
  - chapter: 2
    title: "..."
    sections: [...]
  # ... can have 8, 12, 15, etc.

### Phoenix Raising (V3)
**Status:** ✅ **Supported**

**How it works:**
- num_chapters parameter in plan generation
- Can generate plans with different chapter counts (5, 8, 12, etc.)
- Uses ChapterResolver to resolve safe chapter combinations

---

## 2. Chapter Reordering

### V4 (Omega)
**Status:** ✅ **Supported** (but not actively used)

**How it works:**
- Plan YAML lists chapters in order
- Assembler processes chapters in the order they appear in the plan
- **Can reorder chapters** by changing the order in the YAML

**Example:**
yaml
# Book A: Standard order
chapters:
  - chapter: 1
  - chapter: 2
  - chapter: 3
  # ... 12 chapters

# Book B: Reordered
chapters:
  - chapter: 3  # Start with chapter 3
  - chapter: 1
  - chapter: 2
  - chapter: 4
  # ... different order

**Current limitation:**
- Plan generator always creates chapters 1-12 in order
- Would need to manually reorder chapters in plan YAML

### Phoenix Raising (V3)
**Status:** ❌ **Not built-in**

- No automatic chapter reordering
- Would need manual plan editing

---

## 3. Section Reordering Within Chapters

### V4 (Omega)
**Status:** ❌ **Not implemented**

**How it works:**
- Plan YAML lists sections in order:
  
yaml
  sections:
    - section: 1
      section_id: ch01_sec01
    - section: 2
      section_id: ch01_sec02
    # ... sections processed in order
- Assembler processes sections in the order they appear in the plan
- **No built-in reordering mechanism**

**Current behavior:**
- Sections are always processed in the order specified in the plan
- To reorder, would need to manually edit plan YAML

### Phoenix Raising (V3)
**Status:** ✅ **Implemented**

**How it works:**
- _reorder_sections_by_mode() method
- Reorders sections based on role_order from chapter modes
- Buckets sections by role, then reorders according to role_order config

**Code:**
python
def _reorder_sections_by_mode(
    self,
    *,
    sections: List["SectionContent"],
    mode_name: str,
) -> List["SectionContent"]:
    """
    Reorder prose sections by role-order from a configured mode.
    This does NOT alter beatmap story/exercise placement; it only changes prose ordering.
    """
    # Bucket sections by role
    role_to_sections: Dict[str, List["SectionContent"]] = {}
    for s in sections:
        role = self.section_role_map.get(getattr(s, "section_id", ""), "")
        if role:
            role_to_sections.setdefault(role, []).append(s)
    
    # Reorder according to role_order
    out: List["SectionContent"] = []
    for role in role_order:
        for s in role_to_sections.get(str(role), []):
            out.append(s)
    
    return out

**Example:**
yaml
chapter_modes:
  mode_a:
    role_order: ["HOOK", "SCENE", "REFLECTION", "INTEGRATION"]
  mode_b:
    role_order: ["SCENE", "HOOK", "INTEGRATION", "REFLECTION"]

---

## What V4 Would Need

To fully support structural diversity like Phoenix Raising:

### 1. Chapter Count Variation
- ✅ Already supported (plan structure allows)
- ⚠️ Need: Plan generator that creates plans with different chapter counts
- **Solution:** Use ChapterResolver (already exists) to generate plans with 8, 12, 15 chapters

### 2. Chapter Reordering
- ✅ Already supported (plan structure allows)
- ⚠️ Need: Plan generator that creates plans with chapters in different orders
- **Solution:** Add chapter reordering logic to plan generator

### 3. Section Reordering
- ❌ Not implemented
- ⚠️ Need: Section reordering mechanism similar to Phoenix Raising
- **Solution:** Add _reorder_sections_by_mode() or similar to SectionAssembler

---

yaml
chapters:
  - chapter: 1
    title: "..."
    sections:
      - section: 1
        section_id: ch01_sec01
      - section: 2
        section_id: ch01_sec02
      # ... sections in order
    story_plan: [...]
    exercise_plan: [...]
  - chapter: 2
    # ... next chapter

**What's possible:**
- ✅ Different chapter counts (just list fewer/more chapters)
- ✅ Chapter reordering (just change order in YAML)
- ❌ Section reordering (would need to manually edit YAML)

Phoenix Omega V4 — Structural Diversity & Size-Aware Enforcement Spec
Status: REQUIRED Applies to: Short / Medium / Long books, Normal / Teacher / Teacher Composite modes Non-negotiables: Deterministic, lookup-only, quota-safe, sim-safe

1. Goals (What this must achieve)

Different section orders (role-based)

Chapters

8–10

3. Chapter Count Variation (MANDATORY)
Current State
V4 plan schema already supports arbitrary chapter lists
Assembler already loops over plan.chapters

5. Section Reordering (MANDATORY – NEW)
Problem

6. Section Reordering Rules (MANDATORY CONSTRAINTS)
Section reordering MUST:
Be role-based, not index-based
Be size-aware
Be quota-safe
NOT:
Change section count
Move story/exercise insertion points
Affect teacher attribution
Affect quotas
Run before validation

7. Section Role Map (MANDATORY)

  ch01_sec02: SCENE
  ch01_sec03: REFLECTION
  ch01_sec04: INTEGRATION

Size-Scoped Role Orders

section_modes:
  short:
    role_order: [HOOK, SCENE, INTEGRATION]
  medium:
    role_order: [HOOK, SCENE, REFLECTION, INTEGRATION]
  long:
    role_order: [HOOK, SCENE, TEACHING, REFLECTION, INTEGRATION]


9. Section Reordering Algorithm (MANDATORY)
Implement in SectionAssembler:


def _reorder_sections_by_mode(
    self,
    sections: List[SectionContent],
    role_order: List[str],
) -> List[SectionContent]:

Algorithm
Bucket sections by role
Iterate through role_order
Append sections in that order
Append any unbucketed sections at the end (stable)

10. Execution Order (MANDATORY)

1. Plan resolution
2. Story/exercise selection
3. Quota validation (stories/exercises)
4. SECTION REORDERING   ← HERE
5. Voice bridges
6. Dialect transforms
7. Post-processing cleanup

🚫 Section reordering must NOT happen before quota checks

11. Teacher Mode Compatibility (MANDATORY)
Full Teacher Mode
Teacher quotas enforced
Section reordering allowed
Story/exercise positions unchanged
Teacher Composite Mode
Teacher quotas relaxed
Section reordering still applies
No teacher coverage failures
Normal Mode
Section reordering applies normally
⚠️ Section reordering must not inspect mode — it is mode-agnostic.

12. Determinism Requirements (MANDATORY)
Section reordering must be:
Plan-driven
Config-driven
No randomness
Same plan + seed ⇒ same output

13. Validation (MANDATORY)
Add build-time validation:
role_order references only known roles
All reordered sections still exist
Section count unchanged
Story/exercise counts unchanged
Fail build if violated.

🧠 EXACT PYTHON PATCH (DROP-IN)
1. Schema Update
schema_v4.py


class SectionModesV4(BaseModel):
    role_order: List[str]

class BookPlanV4(BaseModel):
    book_size: Literal["short", "medium", "long"] = "medium"
    section_modes: Optional[Dict[str, SectionModesV4]] = None


2. Section Reordering Logic
section_assembler.py


def _reorder_sections_by_role(
    self,
    *,
    sections: List[SectionContent],
    role_order: List[str],
) -> List[SectionContent]:
    """
    Reorder sections by role order.
    Does NOT change section count or content.
    """
    role_to_sections: Dict[str, List[SectionContent]] = {}
    unassigned: List[SectionContent] = []

    for s in sections:
        role = self.section_role_map.get(getattr(s, "section_id", ""), None)
        if role:
            role_to_sections.setdefault(role, []).append(s)
        else:
            unassigned.append(s)

    reordered: List[SectionContent] = []
    for role in role_order:
        reordered.extend(role_to_sections.get(role, []))

    # Preserve any sections without roles (stable)
    reordered.extend(unassigned)

    if len(reordered) != len(sections):
        raise ValueError("Section reorder changed section count")

    return reordered


3. Wire Into Assembly (Correct Order)
Inside chapter assembly flow:


# AFTER story/exercise injection and quota validation
if plan.section_modes:
    mode = plan.book_size
    if mode in plan.section_modes:
        role_order = plan.section_modes[mode].role_order
        sections = self._reorder_sections_by_role(
            sections=sections,
            role_order=role_order,
        )

⚠️ Must run before:
voice bridges
dialect transforms
post-processing

4. Validation Gate


def _validate_section_reorder(
    original: List[SectionContent],
    reordered: List[SectionContent],
):
    assert len(original) == len(reordered)
    assert {id(s) for s in original} == {id(s) for s in reordered}


5. Minimal Test (Required)


def test_section_reordering_preserves_content():
    sections = [s1, s2, s3, s4]
    reordered = assembler._reorder_sections_by_role(
        sections=sections,
        role_order=["HOOK", "SCENE", "INTEGRATION"]
    )
    assert len(reordered) == 4
    assert set(reordered) == set(sections)

B) Deterministic helpers


def _stable_rng(seed: str) -> random.Random:
    h = hashlib.sha256(seed.encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    return random.Random(int(h[:16], 16))

Chapter count selection


def pick_chapter_count(book_size: str, seed: str, enabled: bool) -> int:
    if not enabled:
        return {"short": 6, "medium": 9, "long": 12}[book_size]

    rng = _stable_rng(seed + "::chapter_count")
    if book_size == "short":
        return rng.choice([5, 6])
    if book_size == "medium":
        return rng.choice([8, 9, 10])
    return rng.choice([12, 13, 14, 15])

Chapter ordering


def order_chapters(chapters: list, mode: str, seed: str) -> list:
    if mode == "fixed":
        return chapters
    rng = _stable_rng(seed + "::chapter_order")

    if mode == "seeded_rotate":
        k = rng.randrange(len(chapters))
        return chapters[k:] + chapters[:k]

    if mode == "seeded_shuffle":
        out = chapters[:]
        rng.shuffle(out)
        return out

    raise ValueError(f"Unknown chapter_order_mode: {mode}")


C) Emit structural diversity block into plan


plan.structural_diversity = {
  "enabled": True,
  "chapter_order_mode": "seeded_rotate",
  "section_reorder_mode": "by_role_order",
  "role_orders": {
     "short":  ["HOOK","SCENE","INTEGRATION"],
     "medium": ["HOOK","SCENE","REFLECTION","INTEGRATION"],
     "long":   ["HOOK","SCENE","TEACHING","REFLECTION","INTEGRATION"],
  }
}

Assembler reads:
if section_reorder_mode == by_role_order: reorder sections using role_orders[book_size]

Then the existing gate reads one format, not scattered conditions.

overwrite:

teacher_exercise_min_per_chapter = 1
Composite Keeps quotas but relaxes “teacher-only coverage” enforcement.

Short answer: no, we’re not breaking the cohesive flow — as long as the guardrails you already specified stay in place. Long answer below, broken down cleanly.

Why the original flow stays intact
The core reason cohesion is preserved is this:
We are not changing the content logic — only the ordering envelope around already-authored roles.
The original book template’s cohesion comes from:
fixed section roles (HOOK → SCENE → TEACHING → REFLECTION → INTEGRATION)
consistent story/exercise placement rules
deterministic assembly (no runtime improvisation)
None of that is violated.

What is changing (safely)
1. Chapter count & order
Safe because:
Chapters are already self-contained units
Each chapter still has a beginning, middle, and integration
Reordering chapters does not change internal chapter flow
Think of chapters like essays in a collection:
Reordering essays ≠ breaking essay logic
Result: macro-flow shifts, micro-flow preserved.

2. Section reordering (the risky part — but handled correctly)
This is where flow could break — but your design avoids it.
Why it stays cohesive
Sections are reordered by role, not arbitrarily
Roles already imply semantic intent:
HOOK opens
SCENE grounds
TEACHING explains
REFLECTION interprets
INTEGRATION closes
Reordering is role-based, not content-based.
So:
You never put INTEGRATION before HOOK
You never put TEACHING after INTEGRATION
You only compress or expand the middle
That’s exactly what Phoenix Raising already did safely.

3. Size-aware stripping ≠ distortion
For short books:
You’re omitting some roles (e.g. TEACHING, extra REFLECTION)
You’re not mangling or truncating them mid-thought
This is critical.
You are doing:
structural subtraction, not semantic mutation
Which means:
Short books feel concise
Long books feel layered
Neither feels broken

Why this doesn’t feel “randomized”
Three important constraints prevent chaos:
Determinism
Same seed → same structure
Role contracts
Sections are authored to be order-flexible within role bands
Quotas
Prevent over-density or emptiness
This avoids the classic “shuffled blog post” smell.

Teacher Mode & Composite Mode are safe too
Full Teacher Mode
Teacher stories/exercises appear more often, but
They still land in the same semantic slots (story beats, practice slots)
Attribution language preserves authority and continuity
Teacher Composite Mode
Teacher content blends with composite content
But quotas keep teacher presence consistent, not sporadic
No whiplash between voices
So flow feels:
“This book has a guiding source” not “This book randomly references someone sometimes”

When flow would break (and you’re not doing these)
Just to be explicit, flow would break if you:
reordered sentences inside sections ❌
rewrote section text dynamically ❌
inserted exercises mid-paragraph ❌
mixed roles without role metadata ❌
allowed runtime generation ❌
You’ve avoided all of these.

Mental model (important)
Think of V4 like this:
Template = musical score
Roles = measures
Structural diversity = changing the setlist, not the notes
Teacher mode = changing the composer credit, not the melody
The song still works.

Final verdict
✅ Cohesive flow is preserved ✅ Structural diversity is safe ✅ Teacher modes strengthen identity, not fragment it ✅ Short/medium/long feel intentional, not hacked
You’re not breaking the book.
You’re doing editorial-level variation, not algorithmic chaos — which is exactly the line you want to be on.

can we integrate dif formats? # Phoenix Raising Format System - Complete Guide

**Date:** 2026-01-22  
**Status:** ✅ Production-Ready

---

## Overview

Phoenix Raising supports **14 different output formats** plus **platform adaptations** (TikTok, YouTube, Podcast, News Articles) through a flexible format assembly system. The system combines:

1. **Generic CSV content** (somatic_generic_with_10_styles.csv) - works for all personas/topics
2. **Format wrappers** (somatic_format_wrappers.yaml) - defines structure for each format
3. **Format assembler** (somatic_format_assembler.py) - combines CSV + wrappers
4. **Platform Adaptation Layer (PAL)** - adapts content for TikTok, YouTube, Podcast, etc.
5. **Module system** - optional extensions like 90-day plans

---

## Core Architecture

### 1. Format Types (14 Total)

#### Format Variants (8 formats)
1. **Standard Book** - Traditional 12-chapter audiobook
2. **7-Day Reset** - 7 daily chapters (teaching + practice + reflection)
3. **10-Day Challenge** - 10 daily challenge chapters
4. **Morning Ritual** - 30-day morning ritual (same sequence daily)
5. **Evening Ritual** - 30-day evening wind-down ritual
6. **Practice Anthology** - Collection of practice exercises
7. **Story Anthology** - Collection of therapeutic stories
8. **Pocket Guide / SOS** - Single short track for emergencies
9. **N-Steps to Result** - Step-by-step guide format

#### Audiobook Formats (6 formats)
1. **Story First** - Story-driven narrative
2. **Step by Step** - Instructional format
3. **Practice** - Practice-focused format
4. **Coach** - Coaching-style format
5. **Episodic** - Episode-based structure
6. **Summary** - Summary/overview format

---

## How Format Assembly Works

### Step 1: User Selects Format Type

python
format_type = "7_day_reset"  # or "morning_ritual", "pocket_guide", etc.
format_mode = "somatic"  # or "expert_base"
format_situation = "panic_attack"  # for pocket_guide

### Step 2: Format Assembler Routes to Format Handler

**File:** SOURCE_OF_TRUTH/tools/somatic_format_assembler.py

python
def assemble_format_content(
    format_type: str,
    persona: str,
    topic: str,
    csv_path: Path,
    wrappers_path: Path,
    style_num: int = 0,
    slot_values: Dict[str, str] = None,
    **kwargs
) -> Dict[str, Any]:
    """
    Main entry point: Assemble format-specific content.
    """
    assembler = SomaticFormatAssembler(csv_path, wrappers_path, repo_root)
    
    # Route to appropriate assembly method
    if format_type == "7_day_reset":
        return assembler.assemble_7_day_reset(...)
    elif format_type == "morning_ritual":
        return assembler.assemble_morning_ritual(...)
    elif format_type == "evening_ritual":
        return assembler.assemble_evening_ritual(...)
    elif format_type == "pocket_guide":
        situation = kwargs.get("situation", "panic_train")
        return assembler.assemble_pocket_guide(situation, ...)
    # ... etc for all 14 formats

### Step 3: Format Wrappers Define Structure

**File:** somatic_format_wrappers.yaml

Each format has a wrapper that defines:
- **Structure** (how chapters/days/steps are organized)
- **Section roles** (what each section does)
- **Intro/outro text** (format-specific framing)
- **Slot placeholders** (for persona/topic customization)

**Example: 7-Day Reset Wrapper**
yaml
seven_day_reset:
  format_type: "7_day_reset"
  description: "7 daily chapters with teaching + practice + reflection"
  
  day_1:
    day_intro: "Day 1: Recognizing the Pattern"
    day_teaching_focus: "Today we'll explore how {book_topic} shows up..."
    day_practice_focus: "A gentle breath practice to help you notice..."
    day_reflection_question: "What did you notice about how {book_topic} feels..."
  
  day_2:
    day_intro: "Day 2: Understanding the Mechanism"
    # ... etc

**Example: Morning Ritual Wrapper**
yaml
morning_ritual:
  format_type: "morning_ritual"
  description: "Same sequence every day for 30 days"
  
  morning_greeting: "Good morning. Welcome to your morning ritual..."
  morning_grounding_intro: "As you wake, notice where you are..."
  morning_breath_intro: "Let's begin with a simple breath pattern..."
  morning_intention_prompt: "What intention would serve you today?..."
  morning_closing: "Carry this intention with you as you move through your day..."

**Example: Pocket Guide Wrapper**
yaml
pocket_guide:
  format_type: "pocket_guide"
  description: "Single short track for emergency situations"
  
  situations:
    panic_attack:
      intro: "You're having a panic moment. Your body is flooded..."
      practice_1: "Emergency grounding breath (4-7-8)"
      practice_2: "5-4-3-2-1 sensory anchor"
      closing: "You're safe. This will pass. Your nervous system is responding..."
    
    anxiety_spike:
      intro: "Anxiety is spiking. You can feel it in your body..."
      # ... etc

### Step 4: CSV Content Provides Base Material

**File:** somatic_generic_with_10_styles.csv

- Contains generic content that works for **all personas and topics**
- Organized by chapter (ch1_content through ch12_content)
- Has 10 style variants (style0 through style9)
- Sections are role-tagged (HOOK, SCENE, REFLECTION, INTEGRATION, etc.)

**Structure:**
csv
section_id,section_name,description,style_num,ch1_content,ch2_content,...
SECTION_01,Hook,Opening hook,0,"There's a sentence you've been saying...","Here's what the sentence has been doing...",...
SECTION_02,Scene,Digital scene,0,"You're scrolling...","You're in a meeting...",...

### Step 5: Assembler Combines CSV + Wrappers

**Process:**
1. Load CSV sections for selected style variant
2. Load format wrapper from YAML
3. Map CSV sections to format structure (e.g., day 1 = teaching + practice + reflection)
4. Apply wrapper text (intros, outros, prompts)
5. Hydrate slots ({book_topic}, {persona}, etc.)
6. Return assembled format-specific content

**Example: 7-Day Reset Assembly**
python
def assemble_7_day_reset(...):
    days = []
    for day_num in range(1, 8):
        # Get wrapper for this day
        day_wrapper = wrapper.get(f"day_{day_num}")
        
        # Get CSV sections for this day's structure
        teaching = get_csv_section(chapter=day_num, role="a4_framework")
        practice = get_csv_section(chapter=day_num, role="practice")
        reflection = get_csv_section(chapter=day_num, role="reflection")
        
        # Combine with wrapper text
        day_content = f"""
        {day_wrapper['day_intro']}
        
        {day_wrapper['day_teaching_focus']}
        {teaching}
        
        {day_wrapper['day_practice_focus']}
        {practice}
        
        {day_wrapper['day_reflection_question']}
        {reflection}
        """
        
        days.append({
            "day": day_num,
            "title": day_wrapper['day_intro'],
            "content": day_content
        })
    
    return {"format_type": "7_day_reset", "days": days}

## Platform Adaptation Layer (PAL)

**Purpose:** Adapts audiobook formats for different platforms (TikTok, YouTube, Podcast, News Articles)

**File:** cluster_therapy_tok/core/platform_adapter.py

### Supported Platforms

python
class Platform(Enum):
    AUDIOBOOK = "audiobook"
    PODCAST = "podcast"
    YOUTUBE = "youtube"
    TIKTOK = "tiktok"

### How PAL Works

#### 1. Platform Compatibility Check
python
compatibility, constraints = platform_adapter.get_platform_compatibility(
    format_name="STORY_FIRST",
    platform=Platform.TIKTOK
)
# Returns: ("high"|"medium"|"low", constraints_dict)

**Constraints include:**
- ideal_length_minutes / ideal_length_seconds
- hook_style (how to start content)
- requires_visual (needs video/imagery)
- requires_subtitles (needs captions)
- fragmentation_safe (can be split into clips)
- safe_fragment_seconds (optimal clip length)
- max_concepts_per_clip (how many ideas per clip)

#### 2. Fragmentation Validation
python
is_safe, warning = platform_adapter.validate_fragmentation(
    format_name="STORY_FIRST",
    platform=Platform.TIKTOK,
    fragment_seconds=60
)
# Returns: (True/False, warning_message)

#### 3. Platform-Specific Adaptations

**TikTok:**
- Short clips (15-60 seconds)
- Hook-heavy (grab attention immediately)
- Visual-friendly (works with video)
- Fragmentation-safe (can split into multiple clips)
- Loop-friendly (can repeat)

**YouTube:**
- Longer format (5-15 minutes)
- Chapter-friendly (can be split into episodes)
- Visual-friendly (works with video)
- Subtitle-friendly (needs captions)

**Podcast:**
- Long-form (20-60 minutes)
- Story-friendly (narrative works well)
- No visual required
- Chapter-friendly (episodic structure)

**News Articles:**
- Text-based format
- Article structure (headline, intro, body, conclusion)
- SEO-friendly
- Shareable format

### Usage Example

python
# Generate book with platform targets
manifest = phoenix_raising_creator.generate_book(
    persona="gen_z",
    topic="anxiety",
    format_type="story_first",
    platform_targets=["tiktok", "youtube", "podcast"]
)

# Manifest includes platform_adaptations
manifest["platform_adaptations"] = {
    "tiktok": {
        "compatibility": "high",
        "ideal_length_seconds": 30,
        "fragmentation_safe": True,
        "safe_fragment_seconds": [15, 30, 60],
        "recommendations": [
            "Split into 15-30 second clips",
            "Add visual hooks at start",
            "Use trending audio format"
        ]
    },
    "youtube": {
        "compatibility": "high",
        "ideal_length_minutes": 10,
        "requires_visual": True,
        "requires_subtitles": True,
        "recommendations": [
            "Create video with b-roll",
            "Add chapter markers",
            "Include timestamps in description"
        ]
    },
    "podcast": {
        "compatibility": "high",
        "ideal_length_minutes": 30,
        "requires_chapters": True,
        "recommendations": [
            "Split into 3-5 episodes",
            "Add intro/outro music",
            "Include show notes"
        ]
    }
}

### Available Modules

| Module Type | Module Name | CSV File |

    self,
    slot_values: Dict[str, Any],
    book_seed: str,
    chapter_num: int,
    persona: str,
    module_type: str = "ninety_day_plan"
) -> str:
    """
    Load module content from CSV and hydrate with slot values.
    """
    # Map module type to CSV file
    module_csv_map = {
        "ninety_day_plan": "module_type_10_90_day_plan.csv",
        "integration_checkpoint": "module_type_11_integration_checkpoint.csv",
        # ... etc
    }
    
    csv_filename = module_csv_map.get(module_type)
    module_path = self.repo_root / "style_bank" / "modules" / csv_filename
    
    # Load CSV and select row deterministically
    # Hydrate slots with persona/topic values
    # Return module text

## Format-Specific Examples

### 1. 7-Day Reset

**Structure:**
- 7 days, each with:
  - Day intro (from wrapper)
  - Teaching focus (from wrapper)
  - Teaching content (from CSV)
  - Practice focus (from wrapper)
  - Practice content (from CSV)
  - Reflection question (from wrapper)
  - Reflection content (from CSV)

**Duration:** 8-20 min per day (60-180 min total)

### 2. Morning Ritual (30-day)

**Structure:**
- Same sequence every day for 30 days:
  - Morning greeting (from wrapper)
  - Grounding intro (from wrapper)
  - Grounding content (from CSV)
  - Breath intro (from wrapper)
  - Breath practice (from CSV)
  - Intention prompt (from wrapper)
  - Intention content (from CSV)
  - Morning closing (from wrapper)

**Duration:** 5-12 min per day (same every day)

### 3. Evening Ritual (30-day)

**Structure:**
- Same sequence every day for 30 days:
  - Evening greeting (from wrapper)
  - Wind-down intro (from wrapper)
  - Wind-down content (from CSV)
  - Body scan intro (from wrapper)
  - Body scan practice (from CSV)
  - Gratitude prompt (from wrapper)
  - Gratitude content (from CSV)
  - Evening closing (from wrapper)

**Duration:** 5-12 min per day

### 4. Pocket Guide / SOS

**Structure:**
- Single short track
- Situation-specific (panic_attack, anxiety_spike, stress_overload, etc.)
- Structure:
  - Situation intro (from wrapper)
  - Emergency practice 1 (from CSV)
  - Emergency practice 2 (from CSV)
  - Emergency

desc how to do: The P1-A/P1-B plan-generator pieces (size-based chapter counts + chapter reordering) aren’t in this repo; add a generator when available. Current changes are assembler/schema only.
If you want, I can add default section_modes role orders to the existing plans to exercise the new reordering path.

Here’s how to implement the missing P1-A / P1-B plan-generator work, plus the optional default section_modes so you can actually exercise the new role-based reordering.

P1-A — Size-aware chapter counts (generator side)

Where: plan_generator.py (or whatever script builds YAML plans).
Inputs: existing persona/topic/duration/seed; add book_size (short|medium|long).
Logic (deterministic):
short: pick chapter count in 4–6
medium: 8–10
long: 12–15
Selection is pure function of book_seed + book_size (e.g., md5(seed + book_size) % len(options)).
Output: write book_size into the plan YAML; emit that many chapter stanzas.
P1-B — Chapter reordering (generator side)

After chapters are generated, before writing YAML:
Compute a deterministic permutation from book_seed (e.g., shuffle with seeded RNG).
Apply to the chapter list only (sections inside chapters stay ordered for now).
Keep anchors if you need (e.g., chapter 1 intro, last chapter outro) by shuffling only the middle band.
No assembler changes required; quotas still apply post-order.
Optional: default section_modes to exercise reordering (plan-level)

Add to each plan YAML (or generator defaults):
section_modes:
  short:
    role_order: [HOOK, SCENE, INTEGRATION]
  medium:
    role_order: [HOOK, SCENE, REFLECTION, INTEGRATION]
  long:
    role_order: [HOOK, SCENE, TEACHING, REFLECTION, INTEGRATION]
Roles come from section metadata type in registry.yaml. Unmatched sections keep original order at the end.
Because the assembler now honors section_modes, this will actually reorder sections per size with no content/count change.
Implementation outline (generator)

Accept book_size param (CLI or config). Default to medium.
Choose chapter count per size (seeded pick).
Build chapter list; optionally set chapter titles as before.
Apply deterministic reorder to the chapter list.
Inject book_size and section_modes block into the plan YAML.
Write plan.
If you want, I can drop in a small helper in plan_generator.py that:

returns chapter_count_for_size(book_size, seed)
returns shuffled_chapters(chapter_list, seed, anchor_first_last=True)
inserts the default section_modes into the plan dict.

Why this is solid (and safe)

✔ No text mutation
✔ No count changes
✔ No role synthesis
✔ No teacher/exercise interference
You’re changing ordering only, and doing it after plan resolution, which preserves all existing guarantees.

Reordering is purely plan-driven (section_modes)
Stable ordering within each role
Seed does not affect section order unless the plan says so
Validation fails fast if membership/count changes
That means:
Sims remain comparable
Rebuilds are reproducible
Coverage gates remain valid
This is critical, and you didn’t break it.

3. Teacher / Composite / Normal modes remain untouched
This is especially important.
You did not:
bypass teacher coverage
merge teacher logic into section logic
introduce mode branching inside reordering
Instead:
Teacher mode continues to control what exists
Section modes control where things appear

Dev Spec — Phoenix Raising Format System integrated into Phoenix Omega V4 (Plan-Compiler Architecture)
Status: Mandatory (core capability) Date: 2026-01-22 Owner: V4 Planning / Plan Generation Non-negotiable principle: Formats must compile into a standard BookPlanV4 before assembly. Assembly remains lookup-only.

0) Goals
0.1 What we are building
Add Phoenix Raising–style formats (7-Day Reset, Morning Ritual, Pocket Guide/SOS, Practice Anthology, Story Anthology, etc.) to Omega V4 without importing Raising’s runtime assembly.
0.2 What “success” means
A format selection produces a fully expanded, valid BookPlanV4.
The existing V4 assembler runs unchanged (or nearly unchanged) on the compiled plan.
Determinism, teacher safety, quotas, and validators remain intact.
Format output is cohesive and consistent, but supports structural diversity (chapter counts, reordering, section mixes) in a controlled way.

1) Non-Goals (explicitly forbidden)
Omega V4 must not adopt:
runtime wrapper assembly
CSV-driven sentence-level selection
pacing/stretch tricks
platform adaptation logic inside generation
any logic that mutates teacher story/exercise content
Platform adaptation remains downstream (PAL) as a post-export stage.

2) Architecture Summary
2.1 Key concept
Format = plan-level structural schema A “format” is a compiler input that generates a normal BookPlanV4. The assembler only sees BookPlanV4.
2.2 Mapping (Raising → V4)
Raising
Omega V4
Format wrapper YAML
Format blueprint YAML (input to compiler)
Format assembler
Format→Plan compiler
Day / step
ChapterPlanV4
Wrapper sections
SectionPlanV4 (role-tagged)
PAL
Post-assembly export step
Modules
Optional appended chapters or format-provided chapter blocks

3) Data Model / Schema Changes (MANDATORY)
3.1 BookPlanV4 additions
File: phoenix_v4/planning/schema_v4.py
Add:


class BookPlanV4(BaseModel):
    format_type: str = "standard_book"  # required for metadata
    format_version: str = "v1"          # for forward migrations (optional but recommended)

    book_size: Literal["short","medium","long"] = "medium"

    # teacher mode: keep existing fields; ensure explicit mode is supported
    teacher_mode: Literal["off","full","composite"] = "off"  
    teacher_id: Optional[str] = None

    # existing: voice/dialect blocks (already implemented)
    voice: Optional[VoiceConfigV4] = None
    dialect: Optional[DialectConfigV4] = None

    # structural diversity knobs (already partially implemented)
    section_modes: Optional[SectionModesV4] = None

Notes:
“Teacher Composite Mode” must be represented by teacher_mode="composite" (first-class).
Assembler must not branch on format_type for assembly logic. format_type is metadata and planning.

4) New Component: Format → Plan Compiler (MANDATORY)
4.1 New file
File: phoenix_v4/planning/format_plan_compiler.py
Public entry point


def compile_format_plan(
    *,
    format_type: str,
    persona: str,
    topic: str,
    locale: str,
    book_size: Literal["short","medium","long"],
    teacher_mode: Literal["off","full","composite"],
    teacher_id: Optional[str],
    seed: str,
    voice: Optional[dict] = None,
    dialect: Optional[dict] = None,
) -> BookPlanV4:
    """
    Produces a fully expanded BookPlanV4.
    Must be deterministic: same inputs => identical plan.
    """

Determinism requirements
All selections are seeded purely by (seed, format_type, persona, topic, book_size, teacher_mode, teacher_id)
No filesystem-order nondeterminism: sort keys, stable iteration.

5) Format Definitions (Input) (MANDATORY)
5.1 Source format YAML(s)
Option A (reuse Raising file directly):
Read somatic_format_wrappers.yaml
Interpret it as plan templates, not runtime wrappers
Option B (preferred for V4 cleanliness): Create a V4-facing format blueprint file:
phoenix_v4/planning/format_blueprints.yaml
This file defines:
chapter count behavior
chapter naming templates
section role sequences per chapter (or per day/step)
optional appended modules (e.g., 90-day plan chapters) — still compiled into plan
Example: 7-Day Reset blueprint (V4 style)


seven_day_reset:
  version: v1
  chapters:
    count: 7
    titles:
      - "Day 1 — Recognizing the Pattern"
      - "Day 2 — Understanding the Mechanism"
      - "Day 3 — Interrupting the Spiral"
      - "Day 4 — Reclaiming Safety"
      - "Day 5 — Building Momentum"
      - "Day 6 — Strengthening the Skill"
      - "Day 7 — Continuing Forward"
    per_chapter:
      role_order: [HOOK, TEACHING, PRACTICE, REFLECTION, INTEGRATION]

Role constraints
Formats may:
omit roles
repeat roles
reduce chapter count
increase chapter count (rituals / anthologies)
Formats may NOT:
introduce new semantic roles at assembly time
splice inside a section body
bypass exercise/story validators or gates

6) Compiler Output Rules (MANDATORY)
6.1 Compiled plan must be “normal V4”
The compiler must output:
chapters: List[ChapterPlanV4]
Each chapter contains:
sections: List[SectionPlanV4] with section IDs resolved
story_plan / exercise_plan entries as applicable
required metadata propagated: book_size, teacher_mode, voice/dialect config
Assembler remains unchanged and uses the plan.
6.2 Section identity strategy
Two safe approaches (choose one; must be consistent):
Option 1 — Role → choose from role library deterministically
Given a role (HOOK/SCENE/TEACHING/etc), select a section asset from an approved library:
deterministic pick from a filtered pool
respects size/mode constraints
stable section IDs
Option 2 — Fixed canonical section IDs per format
Hard-map role orders to canonical section IDs:
simplest, safest, lowest variance
less diversity unless combined with style variants/layers
Recommendation for first implementation: Option 2 (ship faster, safe), then add Option 1 later.

7) Quotas & Modes (MANDATORY)
All formats must respect size-aware quotas for:
Normal mode
Full Teacher mode
Teacher Composite Mode (Teacher Composite Mode)
7.1 Central quota function (single source of truth)
New file or existing: phoenix_v4/planning/quota_policy_v4.py


def get_quota_policy(
    *,
    format_type: str,
    book_size: Literal["short","medium","long"],
    teacher_mode: Literal["off","full","composite"],
) -> QuotaPolicy:
    ...

Policy includes:
stories_per_chapter_min/max
exercises_per_chapter_min/max
exercises_per_book_min/max
teacher_story_min_per_chapter (only for full; optional for composite)
teacher_exercise_min_per_chapter (only for full; optional for composite)
allowed role orders / section_modes defaults (optional)
7.2 Enforcement points
Mandatory enforcement at plan-build time (compiler):
Compiler must produce a plan that can satisfy quotas.
If quota cannot be met structurally (e.g., short pocket guide has 1 chapter, but policy demands 12 exercises), fail early.
Mandatory enforcement at pre-assembly gate (existing V4 gate):
Keep the existing “cannot be wrong by construction” gates.
Add format-aware quota checks if not already centralized.
7.3 Teacher Composite Mode behavior (required)
Teacher Composite Mode (“Teacher Composite Mode”) means:
Teacher content is preferred and counted when present
Missing teacher banks must not hard-fail
Still respects overall story/exercise quotas
Attribution must remain correct when teacher content appears
Implementation: teacher_mode="composite" routes selectors to “prefer teacher bank, fallback allowed”.

8) Structural Diversity Support (MANDATORY)
Formats must support:
different chapter counts
chapter reordering (optional per format)
section role ordering profiles per book size (already supported via section_modes)
8.1 Chapter count variation
Compiler must support chapter counts driven by:
format blueprint fixed count (e.g., 7-day reset = 7)
size-driven ranges (short/medium/long) if the format uses ranges
Example:
standard_book:
short: 4–6
medium: 8–10
long: 12–15
Deterministic selection from range via seed.
8.2 Chapter reordering (format-driven)
Compiler can optionally reorder chapters using deterministic permutation with anchors:
anchor first and last chapters (recommended default for “book-like” formats)
shuffle middle band only
This must be done in the compiler, not assembler.
8.3 Section reordering
Already implemented in V4 via section_modes. Format compiler must populate section_modes defaults per format+size unless overridden.

9) PAL / Export Integration (MANDATORY separation)
V4 outputs canonical text artifact.
PAL consumes the artifact and adapts it for TikTok/YouTube/Podcast/etc.
Action: add format_type, format_version, and book_size into the build manifest metadata so PAL knows what it’s dealing with.
No PAL logic inside assembly.

13) Notes on “Cohesive flow” risk
We preserve cohesion because:
formats change structure only at plan level
sections are role-tagged and come from vetted assets
quotas/validators enforce minimum therapeutic structure
optional chapter/section reordering is bounded and deterministic
Cohesion risk only increases if:
formats allow arbitrary role sequences without guardrails Mitigation: blueprint validation + minimum role constraints per format.

1.2 standard_book blueprint


standard_book:
  version: v1
  description: "Core V4 book. Size drives chapter count and section mix."

  chapter_count_by_size:
    short: 6
    medium: 10
    long: 12

  # Chapter order profile options (deterministic pick by seed)
  chapter_order_profiles:
    - name: canonical
      anchor_first: true
      anchor_last: true
      shuffle_middle: false
    - name: mild_shuffle
      anchor_first: true
      anchor_last: true
      shuffle_middle: true
      shuffle_strength: 0.35   # deterministic partial shuffle; see generator spec
    - name: full_middle_shuffle
      anchor_first: true
      anchor_last: true
      shuffle_middle: true
      shuffle_strength: 1.0

  # Size-aware role orders (used as per-chapter default)
  role_orders_by_size:
    short:  [HOOK, SCENE, TEACHING, PRACTICE, INTEGRATION]
    medium: [HOOK, SCENE, TEACHING, PRACTICE, REFLECTION, INTEGRATION]
    long:   [HOOK, SCENE, TEACHING, PRACTICE, REFLECTION, INTEGRATION]

  # Optional section_modes injection (assembler reordering path)
  section_modes_defaults:
    short:
      role_order: [HOOK, SCENE, TEACHING, PRACTICE, INTEGRATION]
    medium:
      role_order: [HOOK, SCENE, TEACHING, PRACTICE, REFLECTION, INTEGRATION]
    long:
      role_order: [HOOK, SCENE, TEACHING, PRACTICE, REFLECTION, INTEGRATION]

  chapter_titles:
    short:
      - "Recognize the Pattern"
      - "Name the Mechanism"
      - "Interrupt the Spiral"
      - "Build a Small Anchor"
      - "Return to the Body"
      - "Keep Going"
    medium:
      - "Recognize the Pattern"
      - "What Anxiety Is Trying to Do"
      - "The Moment It Starts"
      - "The Body’s Signal"
      - "A Small Reset"
      - "How You Stop Feeding It"
      - "Staying With Sensation"
      - "The New Default"
      - "When It Comes Back"
      - "Continuation"
    long:
      - "Recognize the Pattern"
      - "What Anxiety Is Trying to Do"
      - "The Moment It Starts"
      - "The Body’s Signal"
      - "A Small Reset"
      - "How You Stop Feeding It"
      - "Staying With Sensation"
      - "Your Attention as a Lever"
      - "When It Comes Back"
      - "Identity Without the Spiral"
      - "Practice That Sticks"
      - "Continuation"

Why this works
Cohesive book flow is preserved by role order.
Structural diversity comes from chapter count + chapter ordering profile (optional) + later section pool selection.

1.4 pocket_guide blueprint


pocket_guide:
  version: v1
  description: "Single-track SOS guide. Designed for fast stabilization."

  chapter_count_fixed: 1

  # pocket guide ignores chapter ordering
  chapter_order_profiles:

      anchor_last: true

  situations:

Why this works

practice_anthology:

    short:
      role_order: [HOOK, PRACTICE, INTEGRATION]

      role_order: [HOOK, TEACHING, PRACTICE, INTEGRATION]
    long:
      role_order: [HOOK, TEACHING, PRACTICE, REFLECTION, INTEGRATION]

    medium: "Practice {n} — {topic}"
    long:   "Practice {n} — {topic}"

  practice_progression:
    enabled: true
    pattern_by_size:
      short:  [L1, L1, L1, L2, L1]
      medium: [L1, L1, L2, L1, L2, L1, L2, L1, L1]
      long:   [L1, L1, L2, L1, L2, L1, L2, L1, L2, L1, L2, L1]

2) Quota Policy Specs (mandatory) — phoenix_v4/planning/quota_policy_v4.yaml
This is the minimum enforceable quota model for size + teacher mode + format.
2.1 Common definitions
stories_per_chapter: counts injected stories (teacher or non-teacher)
exercises_per_chapter: counts injected exercises (teacher or non-teacher)
teacher_story_min_per_chapter: only applies when teacher_mode=full
teacher_exercise_min_per_chapter: only applies when teacher_mode=full
teacher_preference_weight: applies when teacher_mode=composite (preference not requirement)

3) Mandatory compiler behavior per format
3.1 standard_book
Use chapter_count_by_size[book_size].
Choose deterministic chapter_order_profile by seed (or default to canonical).
Apply size role order to every chapter (unless overridden).
Set section_modes defaults into plan unless user overrides.
3.2 seven_day_reset
Always 7 chapters.
Chapters always ordered.
Role order fixed (HOOK → TEACHING → PRACTICE → REFLECTION → INTEGRATION).
Apply quotas as defined.
3.3 pocket_guide
Always 1 chapter.
Choose situation (default unless specified) and use role order from situations.
Force at least 2 practice slots in the plan (so quota can be met).
No story slots required.
3.4 practice_anthology
Use chapter_count_by_size.
Role orders are practice-heavy.
Optional intensity progression pattern: compiler writes intensity into each chapter’s exercise plan if supported.

4) Teacher mode interaction (mandatory)
4.1 teacher_mode=full
Enforce teacher-story and teacher-exercise minima from quotas.
All exercise slots MUST be teacher-bank candidates or prebuild fails.
4.2 teacher_mode=composite (“Teacher Composite Mode”)
Prefer teacher bank in selection:
Story: filter teacher bank first; if none, fall back to normal.
Exercise: filter teacher bank first; if none, fall back to normal.
Never hard-fail due to missing teacher bank coverage.
Still must meet total quota counts.
